<div id="review_198304258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198304258" />
    <a title="Rea Cobb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5530091-rea-cobb"><img alt="Rea Cobb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476616479p2/5530091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198304258?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rea Cobb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rea Cobb" href="/user/show/5530091-rea-cobb">Rea Cobb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198304258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13713950537327838597">I love books by Cecelia Ahern, although I always love them I never quite know what to expect next with her books! I have just finished reading The Time Of My Life which is due out 13th October this year. I have to say the cover to this book is stunning and in my opinion is the best cover of all the Cecelia Ahern books.<br/><br/><br/>Plot<br/>Lucy Silchester has received an appointment card. Actually, she’s been invited along few times to this appointment, but she keeps brushing the gold embossed envelope under the </span>
  <span id="freeText13713950537327838597" style="display:none">I love books by Cecelia Ahern, although I always love them I never quite know what to expect next with her books! I have just finished reading The Time Of My Life which is due out 13th October this year. I have to say the cover to this book is stunning and in my opinion is the best cover of all the Cecelia Ahern books.<br /><br /><br />Plot<br />Lucy Silchester has received an appointment card. Actually, she’s been invited along few times to this appointment, but she keeps brushing the gold embossed envelope under the shag pile carpet. She’s taken her eye off the ball and has busied herself with work (a job she doesn’t love), helping out friends, fixing her car, feeding her cat, seeing her family and devoting her time to their life dramas.<br />But Lucy is about to find out that this is one appointment that she can’t miss. And she can’t escape it either. Her life is about to catch up with her in the most extraordinary of ways....<br /><br />My Opinion<br />Our heroine in this book is Lucy Silchester and she is a likeable character who is very down to earth which makes her character easy to read. Lucy’s character is very realistic whereas the storyline is very farfetched but in my opinion it is this great mix which brings the humour into the book. The book gets off to a quick start with Lucy receiving her appointment card from Life which she ignores but she is soon to learn that Life just doesn’t give up on you! <br /><br />Lucy finally meets Life who is a man and although I can honestly say I have never read a character like Life before he is a joy to read. I was expecting Life to be very God or angle like so when we meet a bog standard grumpy guy I was a little shocked! <br /><br />There were many laugh out loud moments in this novel which made it an enjoyable read and very hard to put down. <br /><br />I feel like the storyline carries a message and really gets you thinking, are you making the most of your life and doing things you enjoy? Too many of us, like Lucy have got ourselves wrapped up in life and stuck in a rut and we need to unwind ourselves and make positive changes in life as unfortunately I don’t think Life will be sending any of us an appointment card anytime soon!<br /><br />This book is a must for Cecelia Ahern fans, and does not disappoint. The novel has a great mix of characters who work well together in this book. The novel will give you a very unique storyline which will have you gripped and guessing as to what will happen next all the way through. I loved that the ending wasn’t predictable and also that the ending was tied up beautifully. A truly quirky read !<br /><br />Review also on my blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reabookreview.blogspot.com">http://reabookreview.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13713950537327838597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_317441180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317441180" />
    <a title="Nisha-Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5262009-nisha-anne"><img alt="Nisha-Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442644302p2/5262009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317441180?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nisha-Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nisha-Anne" href="/user/show/5262009-nisha-anne">Nisha-Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5262009-nisha-anne?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317441180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12355557504125865692">This was such a delicious mindfuck of a book, and so very heartrending at the same time. Very early on, I knew this one would hurt. And I kept waiting to feel frustration, even anger at the ways of our protagonist ... but oddly enough, that never happened. Which says something for the skill of Ahern, how she manages to make her protagonists so sympathetic even when they're so royally fucked up. My heart utterly went out to Lucy, to the awful predicament she found herself in, even though I knew o</span>
  <span id="freeText12355557504125865692" style="display:none">This was such a delicious mindfuck of a book, and so very heartrending at the same time. Very early on, I knew this one would hurt. And I kept waiting to feel frustration, even anger at the ways of our protagonist ... but oddly enough, that never happened. Which says something for the skill of Ahern, how she manages to make her protagonists so sympathetic even when they're so royally fucked up. My heart utterly went out to Lucy, to the awful predicament she found herself in, even though I knew objectively that I would abhor and detest her coping mechanism. Hell, I do in real life. But well-written fiction transcends real life, doesn't it? And it's very very true of this novel.<br /><br />What I thoroughly admired was the total unreliability of our narrator's voice. In fact, right from the start I thought "My gosh, this is like Villette." Only nowhere as cold and snobbish, thank christ. Quite the reverse. Luckily, I got her measure very quickly so it was quite easy to tell when she was outright lying to me and when she wasn't. Except for the biggie that kept me swerving one way, then the other.<br /><br />But yes, the mindfuck aspect was totally unnerving and wonderfully so, the fantastic metaphor of it that kept spinning my mind out and reeling it back in and then out again. I can see how that would frustrate so many readers. In fact, I'm surprised I wasn't. But I was just fascinated and even more fascinated, and then even longing for it to be real.<br /><br />How very clever Ahern is.<br /><br />And omg, the Gene Kelly references! Particularly spooky cos the very day I began the novel I was going through a bit of a resurgent love, getting all fatuous and misty-eyed over certain gorgeous pictures and my favourite sequences. For a while there, it seemed liked every pop culture reference Ahern made in this novel was targeted right at me, so closely did our interests and knowledge coincide. Okay, this tailed off towards the end and I am a little disappointed that the Gene Kelly references sort of vanished. But I did love the little touches of Dirty Dancing, that there was just the title and one quoted line in the narrative. I like that Ahern restrained the Dirty Dancing concept really to the concept of our protagonist, the same sort of passive-but-not female protagonist. Pop culture references for the win, darling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12355557504125865692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229143791" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229143791" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1978609-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233429155p2/1978609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229143791?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1978609-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229143791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2547647297185101642">I have read every single one of Cecelia Ahern's books and I love her writing style. I love her elements of mystery and a sort of magic. One of my favourite books is 'A Place Called Here' so when I heard there was a new book by Ahern coming out I had to read it. I was top of the request list at the library (and it's a big list!!!) I knew I would have to read it quite fast, but knew it wouldn't be a problem. I love her books so could get it read in a couple of days.<br/>Lucy's life has gone downhill, s</span>
  <span id="freeText2547647297185101642" style="display:none">I have read every single one of Cecelia Ahern's books and I love her writing style. I love her elements of mystery and a sort of magic. One of my favourite books is 'A Place Called Here' so when I heard there was a new book by Ahern coming out I had to read it. I was top of the request list at the library (and it's a big list!!!) I knew I would have to read it quite fast, but knew it wouldn't be a problem. I love her books so could get it read in a couple of days.<br />Lucy's life has gone downhill, she broke up with her boyfriend of five years, lost her gorgeous apartment, lost her job and got a new one that she hates where she nicknames all the staff and sneaks out for as many breaks as possible. She spends her time trying to avoid family and friends and hides away in her box of an apartment. One day she gets an invite for a meeting with Life - her life. It's time she stopped ignoring her life and started living it.<br />This book was very odd - Life personified is just weird - but it's a weird that works. I was absolutely fascinated. I liked Lucy as a character - she was sassy and had a great with. Her life is great, I actually laughed out loud so many times whilst he was talking.<br />This story will sweep you away but at the same time will have you thinking about your own life and where it's going. And what he/she would look like if it was personified.<br />I love the strangeness of it all and it's overall originality. Ahern charms and intrigues with her writing. I was hooked in and couldn't wait to find out what would happen. <br />There is a bit of a love triangle but in my opinion it's very one sided - I knew who I liked and was shouting at Lucy to be sensible and pick him (I won't say who - it might spoil it for you)<br />It hasn't overtaken as my favourite one of hers but it's quite high up the list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2547647297185101642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer468099927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2646506320354146289">"The Time Of My Life" wasn't an easy read. By that I don't mean I was intellectually challenged, but that I was challenged not to put it down and having to deal with her complaining about her life while still insisting that her life was great.<br/>She was incredibly annoying but somehow I kept going and in the end I didn't regret it. <br/>After the hundred or so pages it took to intruduce the setting (WAY TOO LONG!) it started to all move and shift and the plot developed. That I enjoyed, the end was -thou</span>
  <span id="freeText2646506320354146289" style="display:none">"The Time Of My Life" wasn't an easy read. By that I don't mean I was intellectually challenged, but that I was challenged not to put it down and having to deal with her complaining about her life while still insisting that her life was great.<br />She was incredibly annoying but somehow I kept going and in the end I didn't regret it. <br />After the hundred or so pages it took to intruduce the setting (WAY TOO LONG!) it started to all move and shift and the plot developed. That I enjoyed, the end was -though not brilliant or very satisfying- good enough for me to not regret battling through the boring first hundred-or-so pages.<br />It was an okay book with some good messages.<br /><br />Ich habe es mir mit diesem Roman, "Ein Moment fürs Leben" sehr schwergetan. Über hundert Seiten lang habe ich mich gelangweilt, gehofft dass endlich etwas passiert das die Protagonistin interessanter und v.a. sympathischer macht. Sie steckt in einem Tief fest und kommt nicht los, tut aber nichts gegen dieses Tief weil sie darauf beharrt, glücklich zu sein. Es dauert EINIGE Zeit und VIEL zu lange im Roman dass sie endlich sich weiterentwickelt und etwas TUT.<br />Im Endeffekt bereue ich es nicht, weitergelesen zu haben trotz der extrem unsympathischen und nutzlosen Protagonistin, denn sie tut etwas, sie tut etwas und zeigt dabei dem Leser einiges was er von ihr Lernen kann. Einige gute Moralen sind in diesem Roman trotz seiner allgemein doch irritierenden Hauptcharakterin und langsamen Anfang, daher ist dieser Roman lesenswert.<br />Erwartet aber nicht zuviel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2646506320354146289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n/BQfo/RmCtYxf/NZ4X2mUe7/Ac6NgQ1jEZkIdTPQj90GzgFyD5G1f5sBeyDv3nIAYmxyEbEpeiCeTRS4FI/Ew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kAueZoTnQE/iZgcek7a3TFV7zp6CFZBc3WUXKNTZEMJ74PYdwwiesUTP/T93jDgdE0mDUf7nMYHTWkdb4ERt7g==')})
  }

Recounting the battles fought by five different regiments, the narrative reconstructs the events of the 1965 Indo-Pakistan war, outlining details never revealed before, and remembers its unsung heroes.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"1231176243003616165\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer <span id="freeTextContainer242425968754744027">Cecelia Ahern was born and grew up in Dublin. She is now published in nearly fifty countries, and has sold over twenty-five million copies of her novels worldwide. Two of her books have been adapted as films and she has created several TV series.</span>
